- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls

- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

# Kubernetes RBAC Authorization Flow Security Audit

**Repository:** github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0 (mirror of kubernetes/kubernetes)
**Task Type:** Security Analysis (analysis only — no code changes)

## Scenario

You are a security engineer auditing the Kubernetes API server's RBAC authorization subsystem. Your goal is to trace the complete authorization flow from when an API request arrives to when a permission decision (allow/deny) is made, mapping the attack surface and identifying security controls.

## Your Task

Analyze the Kubernetes RBAC authorization flow and write a comprehensive security analysis. Trace how API requests are authorized, identify entry points where untrusted input enters the authorization decision path, map the data flow through authorization plugins, and assess the security posture of the RBAC implementation.

Write your analysis to `/logs/agent/solution.md`.

## Required Sections

### Files Examined
- List each file you analyzed and its role in the RBAC authorization flow

### Entry Points
1. Identify where API requests enter the authorization subsystem
2. Identify where RBAC policy data (roles, bindings) enters the system
3. Note any places where untrusted input could influence authorization decisions

### Data Flow
Trace the authorization flow through these stages:
1. **Request arrival** — HTTP handler receives the request
2. **Authentication** — Request identity is established
3. **Authorization filter** — Request is routed to authorizer chain
4. **RBAC evaluation** — Role and binding resolution, permission check
5. **Decision** — Allow/deny outcome and audit logging

For each stage, name the specific file, function, and data structures involved.

### Dependency Chain
Provide an ordered list of files from request entry to authorization decision.

### Analysis
- What vulnerability classes could apply (auth bypass, privilege escalation, policy misconfiguration)?
- What existing mitigations are in place?
- What are the security boundaries between authorization plugins?
- How does the authorizer chain (RBAC, Node, Webhook) interact?

### Summary
Concise description of the RBAC authorization security posture and key findings.

## Constraints

- **Analysis only** — do NOT modify any source files
- Be specific — include file paths, function names, and type names
- Focus on the `plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/` and `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/` directories

83-assistanttext-
The analysis has been written to `/logs/agent/solution.md`. Here is a summary of the key findings:

---

## Analysis Summary

### Files Traced (17 files, two main directories)

The authorization flow lives primarily in:
- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/` — HTTP middleware filters
- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/` — interfaces and union chain
- `plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/` — RBAC evaluator and subject locator
- `pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go` — rule/binding resolution
- `pkg/kubeapiserver/authorizer/` — chain construction and hot-reload

### Execution Order (outermost → innermost)

```
WithAuthentication → WithAudit → WithImpersonation → WithAuthorization → API handler
```

`WithRequestInfo` runs even earlier to parse the URL into `RequestInfo`.

### Key Security Findings

1. **`system:masters` unconditionally bypasses all RBAC** — hardcoded as the first authorizer in every chain via `privilegedGroupAuthorizer`. No RBAC policy can block it.

2. **RBAC never returns `DecisionDeny`, only `DecisionNoOpinion`** — it is additive/permissive within the chain. Earlier authorizers (Node, Webhook, ABAC) can grant what RBAC would withhold.

3. **Impersonation headers are a high-value attack surface** — impersonating the `system:masters` group via `Impersonate-Group` achieves full cluster admin if the `impersonate` verb is authorized on the requestor.

4. **Authorization decisions are made against an eventually-consistent cache** — informer-backed listers may lag etcd by hundreds of milliseconds after policy revocations.

5. **The allow-before-error evaluation** (`authorization.go` line 79) means RBAC resolution errors do not block requests that another plugin already allowed — fail-open in multi-plugin chains.

        

      

      

        Tool Calls (39)

  "content": "# Kubernetes RBAC Authorization Flow \u2014 Security Analysis\n\n## Files Examined\n\n| File | Role |\n|------|------|\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/config.go` | Constructs the HTTP handler chain (`DefaultBuildHandlerChain`); wires all filters together |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authentication.go` | `WithAuthentication` filter \u2014 establishes caller identity |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/requestinfo.go` | `WithRequestInfo` filter \u2014 parses HTTP request into `RequestInfo` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/impersonation.go` | `WithImpersonation` filter \u2014 validates and applies identity substitution |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authorization.go` | `WithAuthorization` filter \u2014 the authorization gate; builds `AttributesRecord`, calls the authorizer chain |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/audit.go` | `WithAudit` filter \u2014 records decisions to the audit backend |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/authorizer/interfaces.go` | Core `Authorizer`, `Attributes`, `Decision`, `RuleResolver` interfaces |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/union/union.go` | `unionAuthzHandler` \u2014 chains multiple authorizers; well-known group constants (system:masters, system:authenticated, etc.) |\n| `pkg/kubeapiserver/authorizer/config.go` | `Config.New()` \u2014 instantiates RBAC/Node/ABAC/Webhook authorizers from configuration |\n| `pkg/kubeapiserver/authorizer/reload.go` | `reloadableAuthorizerResolver` \u2014 builds the union chain; supports hot-reload of authorization config |\n| `plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/rbac.go` | `RBACAuthorizer.Authorize()`, `RuleAllows()`, `RulesAllow()` \u2014 the core RBAC decision engine |\n| `plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/subject_locator.go` | `SubjectAccessEvaluator` \u2014 reverse lookup: which subjects can perform a given action |\n| `pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go` | `DefaultRuleResolver` \u2014 `VisitRulesFor()`, `appliesTo()`, `appliesToUser()`, `GetRoleReferenceRules()` |\n| `plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/bootstrappolicy/policy.go` | Default cluster roles and bindings installed at bootstrap |\n\n---\n\n## Entry Points\n\n### 1. Where API requests enter the authorization subsystem\n\nAll requests enter through `DefaultBuildHandlerChain` in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/config.go`. The filter that routes requests into RBAC evaluation is `WithAuthorization` (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authorization.go`, `WithAuthorization` function, line 53). This filter reads the authenticated user from the request context, builds an `AttributesRecord` from request metadata, and calls `a.Authorize(ctx, attributes)` on the union authorizer chain.\n\nUntrusted input that reaches this entry point includes:\n- HTTP verb, URL path, query parameters (parsed into `RequestInfo`)\n- `Impersonate-User`, `Impersonate-Group`, `Impersonate-Uid`, and `Impersonate-Extra-*` HTTP headers\n- Bearer token / client certificate (feeds the authenticator)\n- Field/label selectors when `AuthorizeWithSelectors` feature gate is enabled (parsed in `GetAuthorizerAttributes`, lines 125\u2013149)\n\n### 2. Where RBAC policy data enters the system\n\nRBAC policy objects (Roles, ClusterRoles, RoleBindings, ClusterRoleBindings) enter the system through the Kubernetes API itself and are stored in etcd. The RBAC authorizer reads them at decision time via **informer-backed listers** (cached watches):\n\n- `config.VersionedInformerFactory.Rbac().V1().Roles().Lister()` \u2192 `RoleGetter`\n- `config.VersionedInformerFactory.Rbac().V1().RoleBindings().Lister()` \u2192 `RoleBindingLister`\n- `config.VersionedInformerFactory.Rbac().V1().ClusterRoles().Lister()` \u2192 `ClusterRoleGetter`\n- `config.VersionedInformerFactory.Rbac().V1().ClusterRoleBindings().Lister()` \u2192 `ClusterRoleBindingLister`\n\n(Wired in `pkg/kubeapiserver/authorizer/config.go`, lines 123\u2013128.)\n\nPolicy data is therefore **eventually consistent**: there is a brief window between a policy change being committed to etcd and being reflected in the in-memory cache.\n\n### 3. Places where untrusted input can influence authorization decisions\n\n| Input | Path | Risk |\n|-------|------|------|\n| Impersonation headers | `WithImpersonation` reads raw HTTP headers, parses them into `ObjectReference` structures, then fully substitutes the user identity in the request context before `WithAuthorization` runs | Identity substitution |\n| Field/label selectors in query string | `GetAuthorizerAttributes` optionally parses these into `AttributesRecord` when `AuthorizeWithSelectors` is on; a parse error sets `FieldSelectorParsingErr` but does **not** block the request | Selector injection, mis-parsed allow |\n| URL path | Parsed by `RequestInfoResolver.NewRequestInfo`; misrouting here (e.g., double-encoding) could produce incorrect resource/namespace/name in `AttributesRecord` | Attribute confusion |\n| ServiceAccount username format | `appliesToUser` in `rule.go` (line 281) calls `serviceaccount.MatchesUsername` for SA subjects \u2014 relies on correct username format (`system:serviceaccount:<ns>:<name>`) | Username spoofing if authn is misconfigured |\n\n---\n\n## Data Flow\n\n### 1. Request Arrival\n\n`DefaultBuildHandlerChain` (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/config.go`, line 1004) wraps the API handler with middleware in reverse execution order. The actual execution order is:\n\n```\nWithAuditInit\n  \u2514\u2500 WithPanicRecovery\n       \u2514\u2500 WithMuxAndDiscoveryComplete\n            \u2514\u2500 WithRequestReceivedTimestamp\n                 \u2514\u2500 WithRequestInfo          \u2190 parses URL \u2192 RequestInfo (verb, resource, ns, name, ...)\n                      \u2514\u2500 WithLatencyTrackers / WithTracing\n                           \u2514\u2500 timeout / wait-group / CORS / HSTS handlers\n                                \u2514\u2500 WithAuthentication  \u2190 establishes identity\n                                     \u2514\u2500 WithAudit      \u2190 opens audit event\n                                          \u2514\u2500 WithImpersonation  \u2190 may replace identity\n                                               \u2514\u2500 WithAuthorization  \u2190 ALLOW / DENY\n                                                    \u2514\u2500 API handler\n```\n\nKey data structures produced here:\n- `request.RequestInfo` (struct) \u2014 `IsResourceRequest`, `Verb`, `Namespace`, `Resource`, `Subresource`, `Name`, `APIGroup`, `APIVersion`\n- Stored in context via `request.WithRequestInfo(ctx, info)`\n\n### 2. Authentication\n\n`WithAuthentication` (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authentication.go`, line 46):\n- Calls `auth.AuthenticateRequest(req)` on a union authenticator (tokens, certificates, headers, etc.)\n- On success: strips `Authorization` header and all `X-Remote-*` proxy headers to prevent header injection downstream\n- Stores `user.Info` (interface: `GetName()`, `GetUID()`, `GetGroups()`, `GetExtra()`) in context via `genericapirequest.WithUser(ctx, resp.User)`\n- CVE-2023-44487/CVE-2023-39325 mitigation: anonymous HTTP/2 clients receive `Connection: close` (when `UnauthenticatedHTTP2DOSMitigation` feature gate is on)\n- If authentication fails, calls `failed.ServeHTTP` (returns HTTP 401); the request never reaches authorization\n\n### 3. Authorization Filter\n\n`WithAuthorization` (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authorization.go`, line 57):\n\n**Step 1 \u2014 Build attributes** (`GetAuthorizerAttributes`, line 100):\n```go\nattribs := authorizer.AttributesRecord{}\nuser, _ := request.UserFrom(ctx)           // user.Info from authn\nrequestInfo, _ := request.RequestInfoFrom(ctx) // parsed URL\nattribs.User = user\nattribs.Verb = requestInfo.Verb\nattribs.Resource = requestInfo.Resource\nattribs.Namespace = requestInfo.Namespace\n// ... etc.\n```\nData type: `authorizer.AttributesRecord` implements `authorizer.Attributes` interface.\n\n**Step 2 \u2014 Call authorizer chain**:\n```go\nauthorized, reason, err := a.Authorize(ctx, attributes)\n```\n\n**Step 3 \u2014 Evaluate decision** (lines 79\u201396):\n```go\nif authorized == authorizer.DecisionAllow {\n    // pass through \u2014 NOTE: checked BEFORE error\n    handler.ServeHTTP(w, req)\n    return\n}\nif err != nil {\n    responsewriters.InternalError(w, req, err)   // 500\n    return\n}\n// DecisionNoOpinion or DecisionDeny \u2192 403 Forbidden\nresponsewriters.Forbidden(...)\n```\n\n**Critical behavior**: The allow decision is checked before the error. A comment in the source reads: \"an authorizer like RBAC could encounter evaluation errors and still allow the request.\" This means if the superuser authorizer (or any earlier authorizer in the chain) grants access, RBAC resolution errors are silently swallowed.\n\nAudit annotations written: `authorization.k8s.io/decision` (allow/forbid) and `authorization.k8s.io/reason`.\n\n### 4. RBAC Evaluation\n\nThe union authorizer (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/union/union.go`) iterates authorizers in order. The chain always starts with `privilegedGroupAuthorizer` for `system:masters`, then proceeds through configured authorizers (Node, ABAC, Webhook, RBAC in operator-defined order).\n\n**`RBACAuthorizer.Authorize`** (`plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/rbac.go`, line 75):\n```go\nruleCheckingVisitor := &authorizingVisitor{requestAttributes: requestAttributes}\nr.authorizationRuleResolver.VisitRulesFor(ctx,\n    requestAttributes.GetUser(),\n    requestAttributes.GetNamespace(),\n    ruleCheckingVisitor.visit)\nif ruleCheckingVisitor.allowed {\n    return authorizer.DecisionAllow, ruleCheckingVisitor.reason, nil\n}\n// NOT DecisionDeny \u2014 returns NoOpinion on denial\nreturn authorizer.DecisionNoOpinion, reason, nil\n```\n\n**`DefaultRuleResolver.VisitRulesFor`** (`pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go`, line 179):\n1. Lists all `ClusterRoleBinding` objects via the informer lister\n2. For each binding, calls `appliesTo(user, clusterRoleBinding.Subjects, \"\")` \u2014 checks username, groups, or SA format match\n3. If applies: calls `GetRoleReferenceRules(ctx, clusterRoleBinding.RoleRef, \"\")` to retrieve `PolicyRule` slices from the referenced ClusterRole\n4. If namespace is non-empty: repeats above for `RoleBinding` objects in that namespace, resolving to either a Role or ClusterRole\n\n**`RuleAllows`** (`plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/rbac.go`, line 178):\n```go\nfunc RuleAllows(requestAttributes authorizer.Attributes, rule *rbacv1.PolicyRule) bool {\n    if requestAttributes.IsResourceRequest() {\n        combinedResource := resource + \"/\" + subresource\n        return VerbMatches(rule, verb) &&\n               APIGroupMatches(rule, apiGroup) &&\n               ResourceMatches(rule, combinedResource, subresource) &&\n               ResourceNameMatches(rule, name)\n    }\n    return VerbMatches(rule, verb) && NonResourceURLMatches(rule, path)\n}\n```\nWildcards (`*`) in policy rules are resolved in `rbacv1helpers.VerbMatches`, `APIGroupMatches`, `ResourceMatches`.\n\n**`appliesTo`** / **`appliesToUser`** (`pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go`, line 281):\n- `rbacv1.UserKind`: exact string match on `user.GetName()`\n- `rbacv1.GroupKind`: membership check in `user.GetGroups()`\n- `rbacv1.ServiceAccountKind`: `serviceaccount.MatchesUsername(saNamespace, subject.Name, user.GetName())` \u2014 reconstructs the `system:serviceaccount:<ns>:<name>` username format\n\n### 5. Decision and Audit Logging\n\nThe union authorizer short-circuits and returns the first `DecisionAllow` or `DecisionDeny`. `DecisionNoOpinion` means \"continue to next authorizer.\" If all authorizers return `DecisionNoOpinion`, the final result is `DecisionNoOpinion`, which `WithAuthorization` treats as a 403.\n\nThe audit backend (configured via `--audit-policy-file`) receives:\n- `StageRequestReceived` on entry\n- `StageResponseStarted` / `StageResponseComplete` on exit\n- Annotations: `authorization.k8s.io/decision` and `authorization.k8s.io/reason` set by `WithAuthorization`\n- Impersonated user details if impersonation was performed (`audit.LogImpersonatedUser`)\n\n---\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\nOrdered from request entry to authorization decision:\n\n1. `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/config.go` \u2014 `DefaultBuildHandlerChain` assembles the chain\n2. `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/requestinfo.go` \u2014 `WithRequestInfo` parses URL into `RequestInfo`\n3. `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authentication.go` \u2014 `WithAuthentication` \u2192 `user.Info` in context\n4. `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/impersonation.go` \u2014 `WithImpersonation` \u2192 may replace `user.Info` in context\n5. `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authorization.go` \u2014 `WithAuthorization` \u2192 calls authorizer chain\n6. `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/authorizer/interfaces.go` \u2014 `Authorizer` interface, `AttributesRecord`, `Decision`\n7. `pkg/kubeapiserver/authorizer/reload.go` \u2014 `reloadableAuthorizerResolver` \u2192 `unionAuthzHandler`\n8. `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/union/union.go` \u2014 iterates authorizers; first Allow/Deny wins\n9. `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/authorizerfactory/builtin.go` \u2014 `privilegedGroupAuthorizer` (always first)\n10. `plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/rbac.go` \u2014 `RBACAuthorizer.Authorize` \u2192 visitor pattern\n11. `pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go` \u2014 `DefaultRuleResolver.VisitRulesFor` \u2192 binding/role lookup, `appliesTo`\n12. Informer listers (backed by etcd watch cache) \u2014 supply `ClusterRoleBinding`, `RoleBinding`, `ClusterRole`, `Role` objects\n\n---\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Vulnerability Classes\n\n**1. Authorization Bypass via system:masters**\n\nThe `privilegedGroupAuthorizer` is unconditionally prepended to the authorizer chain (line 98\u201399 of `reload.go`):\n```go\nsuperuserAuthorizer := authorizerfactory.NewPrivilegedGroups(user.SystemPrivilegedGroup)\nauthorizers = append(authorizers, superuserAuthorizer)\n```\nAny authenticated principal whose `user.Info.GetGroups()` contains `\"system:masters\"` receives `DecisionAllow` for every request before RBAC is consulted. This is by design but represents a complete bypass of RBAC: there is no audit trail distinguishing a system:masters allow from an RBAC allow. If a compromised certificate can assert `system:masters` group membership (e.g., a leaked cluster admin certificate), no RBAC policy can block it.\n\n**2. Fail-Open on Rule Resolution Errors**\n\n`RBACAuthorizer.Authorize` collects resolution errors but returns `DecisionNoOpinion` (not `DecisionDeny`) when no rule allows. The filter checks `DecisionAllow` before `err`. Combined with the union chain, if any earlier authorizer (e.g., a misconfigured webhook returning Allow) grants access, RBAC resolution errors are silently ignored \u2014 there is no \"fail closed\" behavior for the RBAC plugin itself. This could mask broken informer state or etcd connectivity issues.\n\n**3. Impersonation Attack Surface**\n\n`WithImpersonation` reads `Impersonate-User`, `Impersonate-Group`, `Impersonate-Uid`, and `Impersonate-Extra-*` headers and substitutes the authenticated user's identity before `WithAuthorization` runs. The filter does authorize each impersonation request against the original user, but:\n- Extra values are URL-decoded after lower-casing in `unescapeExtraKey` \u2014 a malformed encoding silently falls through (line 207: `return encodedKey`)\n- Group impersonation with `system:authenticated` or `system:unauthenticated` is accepted verbatim \u2014 an authorized impersonator can claim or drop these well-known groups by explicit specification\n- `system:masters` can be impersonated as a group if the requestor has `impersonate` on `groups` with the target name \u2014 granting full cluster admin to the downstream authorization\n\n**4. RBAC Privilege Escalation via Binding**\n\n`pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go` provides `ConfirmNoEscalation` (line 52) to prevent users from granting permissions they don't already hold. However, this function is only called during admission control for Role/ClusterRole creation \u2014 it is not part of the authorization path. A user with write access to `rolebindings` (but not `roles`) could bind themselves to an existing powerful ClusterRole without triggering escalation checks.\n\n**5. Policy Misconfiguration via Wildcards**\n\n`RuleAllows` matches `*` in verbs, API groups, resource names, and non-resource URLs. A ClusterRole with `verbs: [\"*\"], resources: [\"*\"], apiGroups: [\"*\"]` grants full cluster admin. Overly broad bootstrap roles (e.g., `cluster-admin` ClusterRole) bound to wide subjects (`system:authenticated`) represent a common misconfiguration path. There is no runtime enforcement checking whether wildcard usage is appropriate.\n\n**6. Informer Cache Staleness**\n\nThe RBAC authorizer reads from in-memory informer caches backed by etcd watch events. A role binding deletion or role restriction may take hundreds of milliseconds to propagate to all API server instances. During this window, revoked permissions remain in effect. This is inherent to the caching architecture but is a security consideration for time-sensitive revocations.\n\n**7. Authorization Config Hot-Reload Race**\n\n`reloadableAuthorizerResolver` uses `atomic.Pointer[authorizerResolver]` (line 70) to atomically swap the active authorizer chain when the authorization config file changes. In-flight requests at the moment of swap may be evaluated against the old chain. The reload loop polls once per minute and validates the new config before applying. There is no mechanism to drain in-flight requests before a reload, creating a brief consistency gap.\n\n### Existing Mitigations\n\n- **Authentication header stripping**: `WithAuthentication` deletes `Authorization` and all `X-Remote-*` proxy headers after successful authentication, preventing downstream forgery.\n- **Impersonation gating**: Every impersonation target requires explicit `impersonate` verb authorization on the appropriate resource type before identity substitution.\n- **ConfirmNoEscalation**: Applied during admission for Role and ClusterRole write operations, preventing users from writing policies exceeding their own rights.\n- **Audit logging**: Every authorization decision (allow/deny) is annotated with decision and reason; impersonation is separately logged with the impersonated identity.\n- **Atomic config reload**: Authorization configuration changes are validated before applying and use atomic pointer swaps to avoid partial updates.\n- **HTTP/2 DoS mitigation**: Anonymous connections over HTTP/2 are forced to close after each request (CVE-2023-44487/CVE-2023-39325 mitigations gated on `UnauthenticatedHTTP2DOSMitigation` feature flag).\n- **Bootstrap policy**: Default roles follow least-privilege where possible; high-privilege bindings (e.g., `cluster-admin`) are not granted to broad subjects.\n\n### Security Boundaries Between Authorization Plugins\n\nThe union authorizer (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/union/union.go`) defines these boundary behaviors:\n- **First Allow/Deny wins**: As soon as any authorizer returns `DecisionAllow` or `DecisionDeny`, the chain stops. A Webhook that returns Allow prevents RBAC from ever being consulted.\n- **No Deny from RBAC**: The RBAC plugin never returns `DecisionDeny` \u2014 only `DecisionAllow` or `DecisionNoOpinion`. This means RBAC cannot block requests that an earlier plugin allows.\n- **Node authorizer is first-class**: The Node authorizer runs before RBAC in the typical `Node,RBAC` configuration, restricting kubelet access using a dependency graph independent of RBAC policy.\n- **ABAC is additive**: ABAC returns `DecisionAllow` for matches and `DecisionNoOpinion` otherwise; it never denies. When combined with RBAC, ABAC can grant access that RBAC would not.\n\n### Authorizer Chain Interaction\n\nTypical production chain (order in `AuthorizationConfiguration.Authorizers`):\n\n```\nprivilegedGroupAuthorizer (system:masters \u2014 always first, hardcoded)\n  \u2192 Node authorizer (kubelet identity graph)\n  \u2192 RBAC authorizer (roles/bindings from etcd)\n  \u2192 Webhook (optional, external policy engine)\n```\n\nA `DecisionAllow` from `privilegedGroupAuthorizer` or Node short-circuits the rest of the chain. The RBAC authorizer is therefore effectively secondary to the system:masters check. Webhook authorizers are configurable with `failurePolicy: NoOpinion` (fail open) or `Deny` (fail closed), directly impacting security posture if the webhook is unreachable.\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\nThe Kubernetes RBAC authorization flow is a multi-layer, pluggable system with clear separation between authentication (identity), impersonation (identity substitution), and authorization (policy enforcement). The core security posture is **default deny with explicit allow**: unauthenticated requests are rejected at the authentication layer, and requests without a matching RBAC policy receive HTTP 403.\n\n**Key findings:**\n\n1. **system:masters is an unconditional bypass.** It is enforced via `privilegedGroupAuthorizer` prepended to every authorizer chain, predates and supersedes all RBAC policy, and leaves no distinguishable audit trail. Compromise of any certificate asserting this group is a full cluster compromise with no RBAC-level mitigation.\n\n2. **RBAC never denies, only abstains.** All RBAC denials are expressed as `DecisionNoOpinion`, meaning earlier authorizers (superuser group, Node, Webhook) can grant access that RBAC policy would not. This is by design but means RBAC alone cannot implement explicit deny rules.\n\n3. **Impersonation is a significant attack surface.** Successfully impersonating `system:masters` as a group value grants complete cluster admin. The impersonation filter is correctly gated by authorization, but the authorization check uses the same pluggable chain \u2014 an ABAC or Webhook misconfiguration allowing the `impersonate` verb could lead to privilege escalation.\n\n4. **Policy data is eventually consistent.** Authorization decisions are made against an in-memory cache; revocations have a propagation delay during which stale permissions remain effective.\n\n5. **Field/label selector authorization is additive.** The `AuthorizeWithSelectors` feature gate extends the `AttributesRecord` with parsed selectors, enabling more granular policy. Parse errors are carried through without blocking the request, which is safe (the error is an attribute of the record, not a hard failure) but requires authorizer implementations to handle the error case correctly.\n\nThe implementation is architecturally sound with defense-in-depth (authn \u2192 audit \u2192 impersonation authz \u2192 main authz), but the unconditional system:masters bypass and the fail-open nature of RBAC (NoOpinion not Deny) mean that the security of the overall system depends heavily on correct configuration of the authorizer chain ordering, webhook failure policies, and tight control over certificate issuance.\n",

Where API requests enter the authorization subsystem\n\nAll requests enter through `DefaultBuildHandlerChain` in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/config.go`. The filter that routes requests into RBAC evaluation is `WithAuthorization` (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authorization.go`, `WithAuthorization` function, line 53). This filter reads the authenticated user from the request context, builds an `AttributesRecord` from request metadata, and calls `a.Authorize(ctx, attributes)` on the union authorizer chain.\n\nUntrusted input that reaches this entry point includes:\n- HTTP verb, URL path, query parameters (parsed into `RequestInfo`)\n- `Impersonate-User`, `Impersonate-Group`, `Impersonate-Uid`, and `Impersonate-Extra-*` HTTP headers\n- Bearer token / client certificate (feeds the authenticator)\n- Field/label selectors when `AuthorizeWithSelectors` feature gate is enabled (parsed in `GetAuthorizerAttributes`, lines 125\u2013149)\n\n### 2. Where RBAC policy data enters the system\n\nRBAC policy objects (Roles, ClusterRoles, RoleBindings, ClusterRoleBindings) enter the system through the Kubernetes API itself and are stored in etcd. The RBAC authorizer reads them at decision time via **informer-backed listers** (cached watches):\n\n- `config.VersionedInformerFactory.Rbac().V1().Roles().Lister()` \u2192 `RoleGetter`\n- `config.VersionedInformerFactory.Rbac().V1().RoleBindings().Lister()` \u2192 `RoleBindingLister`\n- `config.VersionedInformerFactory.Rbac().V1().ClusterRoles().Lister()` \u2192 `ClusterRoleGetter`\n- `config.VersionedInformerFactory.Rbac().V1().ClusterRoleBindings().Lister()` \u2192 `ClusterRoleBindingLister`\n\n(Wired in `pkg/kubeapiserver/authorizer/config.go`, lines 123\u2013128.)\n\nPolicy data is therefore **eventually consistent**: there is a brief window between a policy change being committed to etcd and being reflected in the in-memory cache.\n\n### 3. Places where untrusted input can influence authorization decisions\n\n| Input | Path | Risk |\n|-------|------|------|\n| Impersonation headers | `WithImpersonation` reads raw HTTP headers, parses them into `ObjectReference` structures, then fully substitutes the user identity in the request context before `WithAuthorization` runs | Identity substitution |\n| Field/label selectors in query string | `GetAuthorizerAttributes` optionally parses these into `AttributesRecord` when `AuthorizeWithSelectors` is on; a parse error sets `FieldSelectorParsingErr` but does **not** block the request | Selector injection, mis-parsed allow |\n| URL path | Parsed by `RequestInfoResolver.NewRequestInfo`; misrouting here (e.g., double-encoding) could produce incorrect resource/namespace/name in `AttributesRecord` | Attribute confusion |\n| ServiceAccount username format | `appliesToUser` in `rule.go` (line 281) calls `serviceaccount.MatchesUsername` for SA subjects \u2014 relies on correct username format (`system:serviceaccount:<ns>:<name>`) | Username spoofing if authn is misconfigured |\n\n---\n\n## Data Flow\n\n### 1. Request Arrival\n\n`DefaultBuildHandlerChain` (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/config.go`, line 1004) wraps the API handler with middleware in reverse execution order. The actual execution order is:\n\n```\nWithAuditInit\n  \u2514\u2500 WithPanicRecovery\n       \u2514\u2500 WithMuxAndDiscoveryComplete\n            \u2514\u2500 WithRequestReceivedTimestamp\n                 \u2514\u2500 WithRequestInfo          \u2190 parses URL \u2192 RequestInfo (verb, resource, ns, name, ...)\n                      \u2514\u2500 WithLatencyTrackers / WithTracing\n                           \u2514\u2500 timeout / wait-group / CORS / HSTS handlers\n                                \u2514\u2500 WithAuthentication  \u2190 establishes identity\n                                     \u2514\u2500 WithAudit      \u2190 opens audit event\n                                          \u2514\u2500 WithImpersonation  \u2190 may replace identity\n                                               \u2514\u2500 WithAuthorization  \u2190 ALLOW / DENY\n                                                    \u2514\u2500 API handler\n```\n\nKey data structures produced here:\n- `request.RequestInfo` (struct) \u2014 `IsResourceRequest`, `Verb`, `Namespace`, `Resource`, `Subresource`, `Name`, `APIGroup`, `APIVersion`\n- Stored in context via `request.WithRequestInfo(ctx, info)`\n\n### 2. Authentication\n\n`WithAuthentication` (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authentication.go`, line 46):\n- Calls `auth.AuthenticateRequest(req)` on a union authenticator (tokens, certificates, headers, etc.)\n- On success: strips `Authorization` header and all `X-Remote-*` proxy headers to prevent header injection downstream\n- Stores `user.Info` (interface: `GetName()`, `GetUID()`, `GetGroups()`, `GetExtra()`) in context via `genericapirequest.WithUser(ctx, resp.User)`\n- CVE-2023-44487/CVE-2023-39325 mitigation: anonymous HTTP/2 clients receive `Connection: close` (when `UnauthenticatedHTTP2DOSMitigation` feature gate is on)\n- If authentication fails, calls `failed.ServeHTTP` (returns HTTP 401); the request never reaches authorization\n\n### 3. Authorization Filter\n\n`WithAuthorization` (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authorization.go`, line 57):\n\n**Step 1 \u2014 Build attributes** (`GetAuthorizerAttributes`, line 100):\n```go\nattribs := authorizer.AttributesRecord{}\nuser, _ := request.UserFrom(ctx)           // user.Info from authn\nrequestInfo, _ := request.RequestInfoFrom(ctx) // parsed URL\nattribs.User = user\nattribs.Verb = requestInfo.Verb\nattribs.Resource = requestInfo.Resource\nattribs.Namespace = requestInfo.Namespace\n// ... etc.\n```\nData type: `authorizer.AttributesRecord` implements `authorizer.Attributes` interface.\n\n**Step 2 \u2014 Call authorizer chain**:\n```go\nauthorized, reason, err := a.Authorize(ctx, attributes)\n```\n\n**Step 3 \u2014 Evaluate decision** (lines 79\u201396):\n```go\nif authorized == authorizer.DecisionAllow {\n    // pass through \u2014 NOTE: checked BEFORE error\n    handler.ServeHTTP(w, req)\n    return\n}\nif err != nil {\n    responsewriters.InternalError(w, req, err)   // 500\n    return\n}\n// DecisionNoOpinion or DecisionDeny \u2192 403 Forbidden\nresponsewriters.Forbidden(...)\n```\n\n**Critical behavior**: The allow decision is checked before the error. A comment in the source reads: \"an authorizer like RBAC could encounter evaluation errors and still allow the request.\" This means if the superuser authorizer (or any earlier authorizer in the chain) grants access, RBAC resolution errors are silently swallowed.\n\nAudit annotations written: `authorization.k8s.io/decision` (allow/forbid) and `authorization.k8s.io/reason`.\n\n### 4. RBAC Evaluation\n\nThe union authorizer (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/union/union.go`) iterates authorizers in order. The chain always starts with `privilegedGroupAuthorizer` for `system:masters`, then proceeds through configured authorizers (Node, ABAC, Webhook, RBAC in operator-defined order).\n\n**`RBACAuthorizer.Authorize`** (`plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/rbac.go`, line 75):\n```go\nruleCheckingVisitor := &authorizingVisitor{requestAttributes: requestAttributes}\nr.authorizationRuleResolver.VisitRulesFor(ctx,\n    requestAttributes.GetUser(),\n    requestAttributes.GetNamespace(),\n    ruleCheckingVisitor.visit)\nif ruleCheckingVisitor.allowed {\n    return authorizer.DecisionAllow, ruleCheckingVisitor.reason, nil\n}\n// NOT DecisionDeny \u2014 returns NoOpinion on denial\nreturn authorizer.DecisionNoOpinion, reason, nil\n```\n\n**`DefaultRuleResolver.VisitRulesFor`** (`pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go`, line 179):\n1. Lists all `ClusterRoleBinding` objects via the informer lister\n2. For each binding, calls `appliesTo(user, clusterRoleBinding.Subjects, \"\")` \u2014 checks username, groups, or SA format match\n3. If applies: calls `GetRoleReferenceRules(ctx, clusterRoleBinding.RoleRef, \"\")` to retrieve `PolicyRule` slices from the referenced ClusterRole\n4. If namespace is non-empty: repeats above for `RoleBinding` objects in that namespace, resolving to either a Role or ClusterRole\n\n**`RuleAllows`** (`plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/rbac.go`, line 178):\n```go\nfunc RuleAllows(requestAttributes authorizer.Attributes, rule *rbacv1.PolicyRule) bool {\n    if requestAttributes.IsResourceRequest() {\n        combinedResource := resource + \"/\" + subresource\n        return VerbMatches(rule, verb) &&\n               APIGroupMatches(rule, apiGroup) &&\n               ResourceMatches(rule, combinedResource, subresource) &&\n               ResourceNameMatches(rule, name)\n    }\n    return VerbMatches(rule, verb) && NonResourceURLMatches(rule, path)\n}\n```\nWildcards (`*`) in policy rules are resolved in `rbacv1helpers.VerbMatches`, `APIGroupMatches`, `ResourceMatches`.\n\n**`appliesTo`** / **`appliesToUser`** (`pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go`, line 281):\n- `rbacv1.UserKind`: exact string match on `user.GetName()`\n- `rbacv1.GroupKind`: membership check in `user.GetGroups()`\n- `rbacv1.ServiceAccountKind`: `serviceaccount.MatchesUsername(saNamespace, subject.Name, user.GetName())` \u2014 reconstructs the `system:serviceaccount:<ns>:<name>` username format\n\n### 5. Decision and Audit Logging\n\nThe union authorizer short-circuits and returns the first `DecisionAllow` or `DecisionDeny`. `DecisionNoOpinion` means \"continue to next authorizer.\" If all authorizers return `DecisionNoOpinion`, the final result is `DecisionNoOpinion`, which `WithAuthorization` treats as a 403.\n\nThe audit backend (configured via `--audit-policy-file`) receives:\n- `StageRequestReceived` on entry\n- `StageResponseStarted` / `StageResponseComplete` on exit\n- Annotations: `authorization.k8s.io/decision` and `authorization.k8s.io/reason` set by `WithAuthorization`\n- Impersonated user details if impersonation was performed (`audit.LogImpersonatedUser`)\n\n---\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\nOrdered from request entry to authorization decision:\n\n1. `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/config.go` \u2014 `DefaultBuildHandlerChain` assembles the chain\n2. `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/requestinfo.go` \u2014 `WithRequestInfo` parses URL into `RequestInfo`\n3. `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authentication.go` \u2014 `WithAuthentication` \u2192 `user.Info` in context\n4. `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/impersonation.go` \u2014 `WithImpersonation` \u2192 may replace `user.Info` in context\n5. `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authorization.go` \u2014 `WithAuthorization` \u2192 calls authorizer chain\n6. `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/authorizer/interfaces.go` \u2014 `Authorizer` interface, `AttributesRecord`, `Decision`\n7. `pkg/kubeapiserver/authorizer/reload.go` \u2014 `reloadableAuthorizerResolver` \u2192 `unionAuthzHandler`\n8. `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/union/union.go` \u2014 iterates authorizers; first Allow/Deny wins\n9. `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/authorizerfactory/builtin.go` \u2014 `privilegedGroupAuthorizer` (always first)\n10. `plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/rbac.go` \u2014 `RBACAuthorizer.Authorize` \u2192 visitor pattern\n11. `pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go` \u2014 `DefaultRuleResolver.VisitRulesFor` \u2192 binding/role lookup, `appliesTo`\n12. Informer listers (backed by etcd watch cache) \u2014 supply `ClusterRoleBinding`, `RoleBinding`, `ClusterRole`, `Role` objects\n\n---\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Vulnerability Classes\n\n**1. Authorization Bypass via system:masters**\n\nThe `privilegedGroupAuthorizer` is unconditionally prepended to the authorizer chain (line 98\u201399 of `reload.go`):\n```go\nsuperuserAuthorizer := authorizerfactory.NewPrivilegedGroups(user.SystemPrivilegedGroup)\nauthorizers = append(authorizers, superuserAuthorizer)\n```\nAny authenticated principal whose `user.Info.GetGroups()` contains `\"system:masters\"` receives `DecisionAllow` for every request before RBAC is consulted. This is by design but represents a complete bypass of RBAC: there is no audit trail distinguishing a system:masters allow from an RBAC allow. If a compromised certificate can assert `system:masters` group membership (e.g., a leaked cluster admin certificate), no RBAC policy can block it.\n\n**2. Fail-Open on Rule Resolution Errors**\n\n`RBACAuthorizer.Authorize` collects resolution errors but returns `DecisionNoOpinion` (not `DecisionDeny`) when no rule allows. The filter checks `DecisionAllow` before `err`. Combined with the union chain, if any earlier authorizer (e.g., a misconfigured webhook returning Allow) grants access, RBAC resolution errors are silently ignored \u2014 there is no \"fail closed\" behavior for the RBAC plugin itself. This could mask broken informer state or etcd connectivity issues.\n\n**3. Impersonation Attack Surface**\n\n`WithImpersonation` reads `Impersonate-User`, `Impersonate-Group`, `Impersonate-Uid`, and `Impersonate-Extra-*` headers and substitutes the authenticated user's identity before `WithAuthorization` runs. The filter does authorize each impersonation request against the original user, but:\n- Extra values are URL-decoded after lower-casing in `unescapeExtraKey` \u2014 a malformed encoding silently falls through (line 207: `return encodedKey`)\n- Group impersonation with `system:authenticated` or `system:unauthenticated` is accepted verbatim \u2014 an authorized impersonator can claim or drop these well-known groups by explicit specification\n- `system:masters` can be impersonated as a group if the requestor has `impersonate` on `groups` with the target name \u2014 granting full cluster admin to the downstream authorization\n\n**4. RBAC Privilege Escalation via Binding**\n\n`pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go` provides `ConfirmNoEscalation` (line 52) to prevent users from granting permissions they don't already hold. However, this function is only called during admission control for Role/ClusterRole creation \u2014 it is not part of the authorization path. A user with write access to `rolebindings` (but not `roles`) could bind themselves to an existing powerful ClusterRole without triggering escalation checks.\n\n**5. Policy Misconfiguration via Wildcards**\n\n`RuleAllows` matches `*` in verbs, API groups, resource names, and non-resource URLs. A ClusterRole with `verbs: [\"*\"], resources: [\"*\"], apiGroups: [\"*\"]` grants full cluster admin. Overly broad bootstrap roles (e.g., `cluster-admin` ClusterRole) bound to wide subjects (`system:authenticated`) represent a common misconfiguration path. There is no runtime enforcement checking whether wildcard usage is appropriate.\n\n**6. Informer Cache Staleness**\n\nThe RBAC authorizer reads from in-memory informer caches backed by etcd watch events. A role binding deletion or role restriction may take hundreds of milliseconds to propagate to all API server instances. During this window, revoked permissions remain in effect. This is inherent to the caching architecture but is a security consideration for time-sensitive revocations.\n\n**7. Authorization Config Hot-Reload Race**\n\n`reloadableAuthorizerResolver` uses `atomic.Pointer[authorizerResolver]` (line 70) to atomically swap the active authorizer chain when the authorization config file changes. In-flight requests at the moment of swap may be evaluated against the old chain. The reload loop polls once per minute and validates the new config before applying. There is no mechanism to drain in-flight requests before a reload, creating a brief consistency gap.\n\n### Existing Mitigations\n\n- **Authentication header stripping**: `WithAuthentication` deletes `Authorization` and all `X-Remote-*` proxy headers after successful authentication, preventing downstream forgery.\n- **Impersonation gating**: Every impersonation target requires explicit `impersonate` verb authorization on the appropriate resource type before identity substitution.\n- **ConfirmNoEscalation**: Applied during admission for Role and ClusterRole write operations, preventing users from writing policies exceeding their own rights.\n- **Audit logging**: Every authorization decision (allow/deny) is annotated with decision and reason; impersonation is separately logged with the impersonated identity.\n- **Atomic config reload**: Authorization configuration changes are validated before applying and use atomic pointer swaps to avoid partial updates.\n- **HTTP/2 DoS mitigation**: Anonymous connections over HTTP/2 are forced to close after each request (CVE-2023-44487/CVE-2023-39325 mitigations gated on `UnauthenticatedHTTP2DOSMitigation` feature flag).\n- **Bootstrap policy**: Default roles follow least-privilege where possible; high-privilege bindings (e.g., `cluster-admin`) are not granted to broad subjects.\n\n### Security Boundaries Between Authorization Plugins\n\nThe union authorizer (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/union/union.go`) defines these boundary behaviors:\n- **First Allow/Deny wins**: As soon as any authorizer returns `DecisionAllow` or `DecisionDeny`, the chain stops. A Webhook that returns Allow prevents RBAC from ever being consulted.\n- **No Deny from RBAC**: The RBAC plugin never returns `DecisionDeny` \u2014 only `DecisionAllow` or `DecisionNoOpinion`. This means RBAC cannot block requests that an earlier plugin allows.\n- **Node authorizer is first-class**: The Node authorizer runs before RBAC in the typical `Node,RBAC` configuration, restricting kubelet access using a dependency graph independent of RBAC policy.\n- **ABAC is additive**: ABAC returns `DecisionAllow` for matches and `DecisionNoOpinion` otherwise; it never denies. When combined with RBAC, ABAC can grant access that RBAC would not.\n\n### Authorizer Chain Interaction\n\nTypical production chain (order in `AuthorizationConfiguration.Authorizers`):\n\n```\nprivilegedGroupAuthorizer (system:masters \u2014 always first, hardcoded)\n  \u2192 Node authorizer (kubelet identity graph)\n  \u2192 RBAC authorizer (roles/bindings from etcd)\n  \u2192 Webhook (optional, external policy engine)\n```\n\nA `DecisionAllow` from `privilegedGroupAuthorizer` or Node short-circuits the rest of the chain. The RBAC authorizer is therefore effectively secondary to the system:masters check. Webhook authorizers are configurable with `failurePolicy: NoOpinion` (fail open) or `Deny` (fail closed), directly impacting security posture if the webhook is unreachable.\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\nThe Kubernetes RBAC authorization flow is a multi-layer, pluggable system with clear separation between authentication (identity), impersonation (identity substitution), and authorization (policy enforcement). The core security posture is **default deny with explicit allow**: unauthenticated requests are rejected at the authentication layer, and requests without a matching RBAC policy receive HTTP 403.\n\n**Key findings:**\n\n1. **system:masters is an unconditional bypass.** It is enforced via `privilegedGroupAuthorizer` prepended to every authorizer chain, predates and supersedes all RBAC policy, and leaves no distinguishable audit trail. Compromise of any certificate asserting this group is a full cluster compromise with no RBAC-level mitigation.\n\n2. **RBAC never denies, only abstains.** All RBAC denials are expressed as `DecisionNoOpinion`, meaning earlier authorizers (superuser group, Node, Webhook) can grant access that RBAC policy would not. The impersonation filter is correctly gated by authorization, but the authorization check uses the same pluggable chain \u2014 an ABAC or Webhook misconfiguration allowing the `impersonate` verb could lead to privilege escalation.\n\n4. **Policy data is eventually consistent.** Authorization decisions are made against an in-memory cache; revocations have a propagation delay during which stale permissions remain effective.\n\n5. **Field/label selector authorization is additive.** The `AuthorizeWithSelectors` feature gate extends the `AttributesRecord` with parsed selectors, enabling more granular policy. # Kubernetes RBAC Authorization Flow — Security Analysis

## Files Examined

| File | Role |
